1. The Importance Of Ongoing Research
Alright, now the final thing I want to touch on here as I'm kind of wrapping up this program is
along the lines that research is an ongoing process, okay, and so this isn't something that you
should just do once and be done with, okay? There is so much research to be doing and I want
to, on that note, make sure that research is not all that you're doing because you need to take
action. You need to action this stuff and you need to move quick, right? Speed is the name of the
game. But is this landing page the absolute best version it could be? If you ask me, absolutely
not, okay? There's so much more research that we could be doing to understand even more
about this, right? There is a lot that we need to do in order to even make this even more of an
asset, okay? Depending on the reviews that we start to get or depending on the new offers that
we start to launch or based on maybe understanding something that's maybe more of a pain
point or something that actually came up as I was discussing with the team now that I need to go
and do a little bit more research on is the preservatives, right? Maybe preservatives are
something that I need to draw more attention to and can be something that a lot of people have
concerns around.
And so what I just want to clarify here is that the research process that I did in the beginning
should not just be a one and done process. It's something that as you then gather data and test
the page, you then are able to start to better understand what is working and what's not, and you
can go and do more research around that, okay? And on top of that, the best part about this is as
you start to see, for example, like this angle is working, you can just dive deeper into this, right?
Like if this is working and this is doing well, then just continue to go deeper. Do more on
YouTube, do more on Reddit, pretend that you have this problem and go and try to find those
solutions, okay? And so the main thing that I just want to stress in this rather shorter video,
because I know some of these have been long, is that it's really all about continuous research
and ongoing understanding of your customers and what is happening in the market.
You should not just do this once it'd be done, right? Obviously in the beginning, you're going to do
a lot of research to just even get in the mix of what's happening. But now it's a matter of
continuing to improve your knowledge moving forward. And as you get that new knowledge, and
as you let time do its most wonderful thing, which is like adjust your vision on things, you might
come back through this and be like, why the heck did I even say this? Like, what am I talking
about here? This needs to be way different, right? And so that's the best part about this, and that
should make you excited because this page is not going to be perfect.
Is it converting right now? Hell yeah, it is. Yeah. I mean, come on.
And there's going to be a documentation process that I'm going to walk you guys through that
literally helps. I'm going to show you guys that this is actually going to work. I'm going to
document the thing that we're going to get a page that's going to absolutely crush.

And right now it's already converting right out of the gates, right? But now what we need to do is
we need to do more research because there's probably more that we could do, right? And that's
where the amazing piece of A-B testing comes in and you can A-B test another version of this.
Maybe we cut this story in half, right? Maybe there's some things that we can pull out. Maybe we
pull, you know, and do a little bit deeper and maybe we pull some products that we find.
Maybe we find that a lot of people who thought on this page are ordering like the asparagus soup
or something, right? Like we have the, I think the asparagus shiitake or whatever, right? Maybe
we, maybe we need to get that nutrition label on here, right? There's so much more that we can
do. But again, the whole point is, is that we need to be doing ongoing research. So don't stop the
Reddit research.
Don't stop the YouTube research. Don't even stop the landing page research. What we could
even do is we could potentially now with all of our knowledge, know what's going on.
And now we maybe just come in and we create a new page. Maybe we come in a little bit deeper.
Maybe we write an advertorial.
Maybe we turn this into a different style of a landing page, right? And we can have the same
knowledge, but we can now put it in a different, you know, model in a different, in a different
framework, okay? So it's so, so, so important that you don't just stop once you've, you know, got
something that's working or, you know, you've put in all of this work and now you feel like you're
good. Continue to do the research, continue to think of new ways of how can you make this

Okay. So I just want to make this video to emphasize that this is an ongoing process. You should
not just want and done this.
This is something that you need to continue to do if you want to scale your brand, just like how

The page is the same way. Okay. I want you to start thinking very similar along the lines of

20 EVOLVE - Customer Phone Call Research
All right, guys, so this is something that has come up quite a bit for you guys in chat and Sean
mentioning that he still has brands that are doing a few hundred thousand dollars a day calling
their customers. And this is something that really can unlock a lot of gold for you because you
can just simply have a phone call with someone and learn a little bit more about their journey and
what's going on, okay? With that said, you don't want to call this person and start bombarding
them with questions or say like, hey, do you mind if I ask you some questions or anything like
that? You want to approach it very casually and you just want to have a conversation, okay? So
any customer that has placed a higher than average purchase order on your site, and again, if
you don't know how to find that, you go into your Shopify admin, you go to orders and if you click
on that person, you should be collecting their phone number. If you are not collecting their phone
number, then just Google how to collect phone numbers.
I'm not going to show you guys how to do that here. It's very simple to do. You can just enable
that people actually give you their phone number and then you can obviously go ahead and call
them, okay? So it's very simple to do.
With that said, whenever someone places an order, say your average order value is $60 and
someone buys like four or five of them or something like that, that is a great person to go and call
because you might learn a little bit more about why they're buying so many. But on top of that,
you can also just call people who have purchased maybe once or purchased twice. If you have a
repeat customer, you could call them or if you just have someone that has just placed an order
and you want to call them, you could do that as well, okay? So the first thing that you're going to
do is you're going to just call them, cold call them, pull up your phone, say, Hey, name, you know,
it's your name calling from your brand is now about time to talk.
Okay. Very simple to give you guys an example here. Here it goes back to OG Spencer cold
calling days, you know, Hey Jack, it's Spencer calling from EZA is now about time to talk.
And when you leave it that way, you're gonna get one or two answers. One they're going to say,
yeah, actually I'm just in the middle of something. Do you mind if you call me back? Right? And
you can obviously go ahead and schedule a time to call them back.
Or two, there's like, no, I've got, I'm good. What's up? Right. And they'll probably answer.
Because again, if you say that it's you like Spencer from EZA and they just purchased an order or
a, it's a, you know, it's Spencer from aloe yoga. They're probably cause they just placed an order
going to be like, Oh, what's this about? Right? So it'd be like, no, no, no. What's, what's going on.
And so if they do that, then you can say, you know, I saw you just placed an order with us and I
wanted to one just personally reach out and thank you for supporting our brand. But two, I just
wanted to ask if you could explain a little bit more about how you, how you got to our brand.

Right.
And you want to leave it there. You want to pause. You don't want to say anything else.
You just want them to start talking about how they actually got to your brand. And if they ask like,
Oh, like, like, what do you mean? How I got to the brand? Then you can obviously explain a little
bit further. It's like, Oh, I'm just looking to, you know, better understand, like, how'd you find out
about us? Like, you know, what, what were you looking for? And you can start to reiterate there.
But ultimately what you're trying to do is you're trying to get them to talk as long as possible.
Okay. The ideal answer that you get from this is you are like, or you ask that question and they're
like, Oh, well, you know, I was recently, you know, rebuilding my patio and I was super tired of,
you know, trying to, you know, use these, you know, this, this paint finisher or whatever the hell it
is that you sell.
And you know, it kept getting dry and messing things up and not looking the way that I wanted to.
And, you know, I tried going to a bunch of different stores in person, but that didn't really work.
And so then I started looking online and I saw that you guys, you know, I saw one of your ads on
Facebook, which is probably going to happen.
And I really liked the ad and I thought, you know, okay, I'll go check these guys out and give it a
try. And so, you know, that's why I bought. So that's, that's, you know, that's the journey, right?
And so now what you can understand is you're gonna get a lot of different, you know, pain points
from that.
And you can continue the conversation further and be like, Oh, okay. So you tried X, Y, and Z
like, okay, well, what about, you know, our brand specifically? And you can just have a
conversation, but this is how you want to start it. You don't want to like pepper them with
questions, be like, you know, you don't want to be like, what's your favorite color? You know,
what's this? What's that? Like, you don't want to ask them a bunch of questions or like, what are
you in pain about? Or like, what are you hoping to get out of this? Right? Like, what are the
benefits of our product? Like, you don't want to ask that dumb stuff.
Like you want to just have a conversation. And this is where you can ask them, like, if you could
just explain a little bit more about how you got to our brand, that would be extremely helpful for
you to understand the customer journey. Because once you understand the customer journey,
you can ideally recreate it and you can know the different problems that they're going through and
they'll just automatically start talking about it.
Okay. So again, let them talk for as long as possible, jot down some notes, make sure you have a
pen and paper with you or make sure you're, you know, you're typing away and make sure you
store these notes again in your research doc or elsewhere. Okay.

Again, you're really just looking to better understand their journey, what they're looking for and
some of the things that they were potentially going through that ultimately made them purchase
your product. Okay. So that is how you can phone call customers.
Again, this is not a word for word script that you have to follow, but this is something that will work
well. It's based off of basic cold calling principles, but at the same time, you're not really cold
calling, you're kind of warm calling because they've already given you their credit card. So
whenever you call them and you're like, Hey, it's, you know, Spencer from Alloyoga, like just
wanted to, you know, it's now a bad time, right? They're going to be pretty receptive to that.
Okay. So that is how you can do that. If you have any questions, obviously you can ping them in
the chat, but we'd love to see you guys starting to cold call some of your customers as well, warm
call some of your customers to get data as well.

FILE: Alternative Solution Research _ PCOS Women with Hair loss _ MasterClass .docx.txt

Alternative Solution Research

​
The purpose of Alternative Solution Research is to deeply understand the solutions
our avatar has already tried, capturing their genuine opinions, preferences, frustrations,
and objections. ​
This research reveals precisely what our avatar dislikes—or even hates—about
competing solutions, providing strategic insights on how to position our solution as the
superior, preferred alternative.
Additionally, this analysis serves as valuable inspiration for developing ad concepts that
directly challenge these competing products. For instance, if our avatar dislikes
Minoxidil due to poor results for PCOS-related hair loss, we can create a compelling ad
concept around:
"Why Minoxidil Isn't Working for Your PCOS Hair Loss—And What
Actually Does."
This immediately addresses our avatar's frustrations, educates them about why
alternatives fall short, and clearly positions our solution as the Best and only real
solution.

AI PROMPT ​
​
​
Hi, I want you to act as a world-class creative strategist for a $100M/year direct response brand
in the [NICHE]. Your mission is to thoroughly analyze and extract detailed, emotional, and
insight-driven responses from the provided raw data—real discussions, reviews, and
experiences shared by our ideal customer (the AVATAR).
Carefully read and deeply analyze each provided document. Your objective is to answer these
specific questions based on the avatar’s unfiltered discussions:
1.​ What Alternative Solutions or Products Has the Avatar Already Tried?
○​ Clearly list each mentioned alternative solution or product.
2.​ What Positive Experiences or Benefits Has the Avatar Mentioned About These
Alternative Solutions?
○​ Include direct quotes from the avatar about any perceived benefits or successes.
3.​ What Specific Frustrations, Disappointments, or Complaints Has the Avatar
Expressed About These Alternative Solutions?
○​ Capture exact frustrations or complaints expressed in the avatar’s own language.
4.​ Which Solution Does the Avatar Currently Perceive as the Best Option, and What
Reasons Do They Give for This Choice?
○​ Clearly identify the solution currently preferred by the avatar, supported by their
explicit reasoning from direct quotes.
5.​ How Can We Strategically Position Our Solution as the Clearly Superior Option,
Based on Insights Gained from Analyzing the Avatar's Experiences with
Alternative Solutions?
○​ Provide actionable insights and strategic positioning advice directly informed by
the avatar’s stated experiences, frustrations, and perceived best options.
Structure your responses clearly under each question category, using direct quotes and concise,
insightful summarizations. Prioritize clarity, specificity, and direct actionable insights.

The purpose of conducting an Avatar Deep Dive is to understand our ideal

we create a powerful advantage over the market, allowing us to craft highly
personalized ads, landing pages, and offers that speak directly to their emotions,
pain points, and desires.

FILE: Big_Swing_Framework.txt

Big Swing Framework

THE BIG SWING FRAMEWORK
BY ZAKARIA_AIRAKAZ​

How to Iterate Now That Meta Changed the Game

WHAT HAPPENED
Late 2024, Meta dropped this update called Andromeda. Changed everything.
Here's the thing Meta now looks at your ads and scores how similar they are. If two ads look
too much alike, same vibe, same style, Meta goes "that's the same ad" and groups them
together.
So all that stuff we used to do?
•​
•​
•​
•​
•​

New headline on the same video? Meta sees it as same ad.
Different thumbnail? Same ad.
New hook, same body? Same ad.
Same creator, different script? Same ad.
Different colors? Same ad.

That old iteration game is dead. Meta sees right through it.

SO HOW DO YOU ITERATE NOW?
Meta groups ads by how they LOOK. So you need ads that look genuinely different.
Different format. Different messenger. Different story. Different hook. That's iteration
in 2025.
OLD WAY (Dead)
Same format, new headline
Same creator, new script
Same style, different colors
New thumbnail
Hook swaps
Meta: "Same ad, not testing"

NEW WAY (This Works)
UGC → VSL
Regular person → Expert
Discovery story → Warning story
Selfie video → Text wall
Completely different execution
Meta: "New ad, let's test it"

WHERE THE DECONSTRUCTION FITS
The Winner Ad Deconstruction is your learning tool. It's how you build a dataset of what
actually works.
When you break down a winning ad, you're studying WHY it works: ​
the structure, the transitions, the avatar psychology, the belief shifts, the proof sequence, the
emotional journey, all of it.
That deep understanding is what lets you come up with better hypotheses. Better angles to
test. Better ads to create.
The deconstruction builds your understanding. From that understanding, you create.

Page 1

Big Swing Framework

WHAT'S AN ANGLE
The angle is the psychological entry point. It's how you start the conversation. It's the reason
someone stops scrolling and pays attention.
Different angles hit different people:
•​
•​
•​
•​
•​

"Your bloating isn't about food — it's your gut bacteria" → mechanism angle
"Dermatologists have been lying to you" → enemy/exposé angle
"I tried everything for 10 years until this" → struggle/discovery angle
"This is what [expert] uses but won't tell you" → secret/insider angle
"Your hair loss has nothing to do with genetics" → reframe angle

The "they lied to you" angle hits skeptics. The "I struggled for years" angle hits people
who've tried everything. The "here's the science" angle hits logical buyers.
Different angles = different slices of your TAM.

WHAT'S AN EXECUTION
The execution is HOW you deliver the angle. Same angle can be delivered a hundred
different ways.

Formats
•​
•​
•​
•​
•​
•​
•​
•​

UGC — someone in their bathroom telling the story
VSL — Educational content doing the talking
Talking head — expert or founder on camera
Testimonial mashup — bunch of people
Demo — just show the product working
Text wall — story written over b-roll
Interview — like a podcast clip
Reaction — responding to something

Messengers
•​
•​
•​
•​
•​
•​

Regular person who struggled
Expert or doctor
Skeptic who got convinced
Founder
Super fan
Multiple people — mashup

Stories
•​
•​
•​
•​
•​
•​

Discovery — "how I found this"
Struggle — "everything I tried before"
Warning — "what happens if you don't"
Comparison — "why this not that"
Secret — "what they don't want you to know"
Transformation — "before vs after"

Hooks
•​

Question — "Did you know...?"
Page 2

Big Swing Framework

•​
•​
•​
•​
•​

Shock — "I can't believe I'm saying this..."
Call-out — "If you have [problem]..."
Story — "6 months ago I was..."
Curiosity — "This is what finally..."
Controversy — "[Industry] has been lying..."

1 angle × 8 formats × 6 messengers × 6 stories × 6 hooks = hundreds of genuinely
different ads
Meta sees them as different because they ARE different. Different look, different feel,
different energy.

ALWAYS HUNTING FOR NEW ANGLES
While you're running your angles every way, you're also looking for new angles. Always.
Not because the old ones stopped working. Because more angles = more TAM = more
scale.
Each angle reaches a different slice of your market. The more angles you have, the more of
your TAM you can reach.
So you're always hunting.
Where to find new angles:
•​
•​
•​
•​
•​

Your Survey — gives you ideas for new angles to test
Competitor ads — what angles are they running that you haven't tried?
Customer language — reviews, comments, DMs angles hiding in their words
Flip it — if your angle is fear, try hope. Emotional? Try logical.
Different entry points — health vs vanity, save time vs save money, gain vs stop
losing

THE GAME
Two things happening at the same time. Always.
1.​ Run your winning angles through every execution
2.​ Hunt for new angles to expand TAM
Not one then the other. Both. All the time.
That's how you scale.

THE WORKFLOW
3.​ Study winning ads — use the deconstruction to build deep understanding
4.​ Come up with hypotheses — what angles could work? What should you test?
5.​ Run each angle every way — formats, messengers, stories, hooks
6.​ Double down on what pops — scale the winning combos
7.​ Keep hunting for new angles — more angles = more TAM
8.​ Stack angles — multiple angles running, each in multiple executions

Page 3

Big Swing Framework

DON'T DO THIS
•​
•​
•​
•​

Don't make "variations" — same format + new headline is dead. Meta groups it.
Don't kill angles too fast — if UGC flopped, try diffrent story before you give up on
the angle
Don't stop hunting — even when stuff is working. More angles = more scale.
Don't run one angle one way — every angle should be in multiple executions at
once

BOTTOM LINE
Meta killed the old iteration game. Small tweaks, same format, new headline, they group all
that together. Dead.
New iteration = genuinely different executions.
Use the deconstruction to learn. Come up with angles to test. Run each angle through every
format, messenger, story, hook.
While you're running, hunt for new angles. More angles = more TAM = more scale.
That's the game now. Go run it.

Page 4

FILE: Competitor Research Analyse _ Master Class _1_.docx.txt
======================================================================

Competitor Research Analyse​

​
​

The goal of Competitor Research is to deeply understand what leading competitors'
brands in our space are doing — what they’re doing well, where they’re falling short,
and how they’re converting customers across their funnel.

This research helps us:
●​

✅ Pinpoint what angles, offers, and ad formats are performing best in the
market (what to test or improve in our own funnel)​

●​

✅ Identify weak spots or blind spots in their strategy (what we can exploit or
do better)​

●​

✅ Uncover opportunities to craft ads and offers thats are better than them

⚠️ This is not about mimicking or copying competitors.

It’s about understanding how they run — what’s working, what’s failing — so we can
make smarter, more informed creative and strategic decisions.
The goal is to build a better, more unique funnel and ads — not a similar one.​

My best performing ad so far is a native static ad but I don't see many brands in my niche running that specific creative format that I can mimic. The inspiration for that creative came from another brand in the beauty/skincare niche. I was wondering if it's better to double down with deeper sub-avatars using that same format that worked for me (that isn't widely used in my niche/by competitors) or just copy competitors.

Thank you!

FILE: For the 1M_m _2_ _1.txt
======================================================================

Redefine the Founder Role (You)
Once you're at $1M/month, the worst thing you can do is stay the bottleneck.
Your priorities now:
●​
●​
●​
●​

Drive strategic growth: Identify new avatars, new offers, and new channels.
Install leadership: Hire or promote strong CMO, COO
Build org clarity: Restructure roles, remove overlaps, define decision-making power.
Review profit weekly: Not revenue. Not spend. Profit.
"Your job is no longer doing. It's designing. The company is the product now."

As CMO:
Be behind the creative team not doing their job, but guiding vision, angles, trends.
Research what’s working across other niches to stay ahead of the curve
Always ask:
→ Can we introduce a new avatar?
→ What emotional angles haven’t we touched yet?
→ What’s stale or predictable in our messaging?
​
​
New Avatar Discovery
●​ → Who else has this problem but isn’t currently buying from us?​
●​ → What underserved communities or identity groups could relate to this offer if
messaged differently?​
●​ → What different belief systems (health, money, relationships) would make someone
want this even more?​
●​ → How would we sell this to a completely different age group, profession, or lifestyle?​

Emotional Angle Expansion
●​ → What does buying this help them feel, not just what it does?​

●​ → What core fear, insecurity, or frustration does this product quietly solve?​
●​ → What “identity” are they stepping into by purchasing?​
●​ → What would make them feel proud to buy this, not guilty or skeptical?​
●​ → What are they secretly ashamed to talk about , but our product can address that
without calling it out?​

Market Positioning & Narrative Power
●​ → What are people sick of hearing from every brand in our space?​
●​ → If we were launching today in a crowded space, how would we disrupt it?​
●​ → What core belief do we hold that no one else is saying out loud?​
●​ → What myths or misconceptions could we publicly challenge, and win?​
●​ → How would we sell this if we had no testimonials or social proof? (forces presell
clarity)​

Funnel / LP / Angle Innovation
●​ → Can this be reframed as a lifestyle, not a product?​
●​ → How would we sell this if it was a $5K product? (forces deeper value clarity)​
●​ → What is the invisible “before/after” we’re not showing clearly enough on LPs?​
●​ → Are we talking too much about the product, and not enough about the transformation?​
●​ → What promise would make someone stop scrolling, even if they didn’t know they had
the problem yet?​

Is it time to start pushing some top-of-funnel to reach the unaware part of our audience?

●​ → What would speak to someone who doesn’t even know they have a problem yet?​
●​ → What’s a curiosity or insight angle that would hook someone who’s aware but not
actively searching?​
●​

What “movement” or belief can we attach the product to, so it feels bigger than a
transaction?​

Oversee the funnel not the buttons, but the psychology and congruency.

As CEO:
This is where you shift from “doing” to designing the org that scales itself.​

1. Build Pods Around Specific Avatars
●​ Start building dedicated pods around each core customer avatar so each team deeply
understands that persona, their problems, and how to speak to them.​
●​ Each pod should own creative, funnel, angles, and retention tailored to that avatar.​

Once you validate a new avatar, spin up a new pod to crack and scale it then let
that pod lead its growth lane.
When you’ve got 2+ pods running, that’s your signal to bring in a CMO to oversee
and optimize the system.

2. Strategic Hires
●​ Bring in COO to fully own ops and backend scaling.​
●​ CMO or Head of Growth to direct pods, creative testing, and avatar expansion.​
●​ Head of Brand to raise storytelling, positioning, and cross-channel brand consistency.​

3. New Channels & Partnerships

●​ Expand into new acquisition or distribution layers:​
○​ GADS​
○​ TikTok Shop if possible for you​
○​ Amazon​
○​ Native (if aligned with the brand) later on ​

4. Product Expansion & Innovation
●​ Introduce new SKUs to:​
○​ Unlock new avatars​
○​ Increase AOV/LTV​
○​ Create entry-level offers or bundles​
●​ R&D or reposition existing products to:​
○​ Stay ahead of market sophistication (e.g., avoid “sounding like everyone else in
the market.” positioning)​
○​ Refresh angles for ad fatigue or creative burnout​
○​ Stay culturally relevant, and align with evolving language, trends, or social trend​
○​ Solve conversion drop-offs or improve perceived value, even in one-time
purchase models​

5. Backend & Exit Readiness
●​ Clean up financials, contracts, and operations for optional exit.​
●​ Improve reporting, SOPs, margin clarity, and reduce key-person risk.

Live Product Research w/ Kalodata - Pt 2

59:45

**Checklist from the video:**  
1) For this method we're using a paid tool [https://www.kalodata.com/signup?tc=evolve10](https://www.kalodata.com/signup?tc=evolve10 "https://www.kalodata.com/signup?tc=evolve10"). Code: evolve10 for 10% off. Kalodata is a tool that pulls the best performing TikTok shop products.

2) Filter at the product level. Last 7 days, Avg unit price >$15, sales growing rapidly.

3) Any of the products here not attached to a big brand (E.g. Goli, Shark, Comfrt) has the potential to be sold.

4) Go through the listings and look into the brand to verify if it is a big brand. Do a Google search, check their social media following. If they're a established brand they can easily afford litigation to take you down. Not worth it running bootleg versions.

5) Check the trademark websites on wherever you plan to sell to verify if the brand/product name has a trademark. For example in the US you may use [https://tmsearch.uspto.gov/search/search-information](https://tmsearch.uspto.gov/search/search-information "https://tmsearch.uspto.gov/search/search-information") (Free) or GPT/Claude to find out. If the product is called "Blood Elixir" and all the TT videos mention it, if you reuse those clips with product name mention there's a higher risk of getting taken down. In that case obviously use a different brand name and also different product name. Trademarked doesn't mean you can't sell the product, just means you can't use certain phrases on the site and ads.

6) Use [https://pro.similarweb.com/](https://pro.similarweb.com/ "https://pro.similarweb.com/") (Free) to estimate how much the store is doing. Always be more conservative. Let's say the average is 1% conversion rate (CVR). Estimate the AOV based on product selling price. Website visitors x CVR x AOV = Estimated Revenue. For this prod research method, the estimated revenue on the site is less important as some stores do a lot with TTS but not on their own website. Product can still sell via FB ads.

7) Do some basic research on the product. Go through the top performing videos from Kalodata TikTok shop videos and the comments. See what's the current angle they're targeting, who they're targeting, what the comments are saying.

8) Also go through [https://www.facebook.com/ads/library](https://www.facebook.com/ads/library "https://www.facebook.com/ads/library") and [https://tryatria.com/?linkId=lp\_879287&sourceId=shaun-eng&tenantId=atria](https://tryatria.com/?linkId=lp_879287&sourceId=shaun-eng&tenantId=atria "https://tryatria.com/?linkId=lp_879287&sourceId=shaun-eng&tenantId=atria") (Paid tool - Optional) to see what the competition is running.

9) Do more research based on the subsequent modules on how to find your avatar. Wherever possible - Google search, YT videos, IG reels, Tiktok videos. We know there's only 2 ways to win if you're not first to market. A new mechanism or an underserved avatar. The subsequent module will cover the avatar side. Our goal with this research is to find if we can find new angles, mechanisms, or avatars we can target besides what the competition is doing so you can stand out. So we need to know what types of angles your current competition is running and the current market sophistication level.

10) Check with supplier if the pricing they can get makes sense. You want to use tools like Claude, GPT or Amazon to check what is the average price for the product you're going to sell so it's reasonable and within expectation. If you're selling super premium prices but only sell cheap low quality products it won't go well. After getting a quote or checking on AliExpress, see if you 3x'd the COGS (cost of goods) + Shipping, if the product still falls under the expected price range. E.g. $20 COGs total, $60 selling price, $40-60 is expected price based on Claude/Amazon.

11) After you found a potential product, all you need to do is rip the top 10-20 best performing (by revenue) videos that Kalodata shows, and run it alongside your own creatives you made based on research.  
  
Note:  
For brand new beginners, I do not recommend starting out with a higher ticket item like the 1st product in the video at $100+ product price. Starting out, finding finding products you can sell for $40-80 is good  
  
And also, you can't rely on the ripped creatives to scale long term. Treat it as borrowed time. It's only a matter of time until it dies or gets taken down, even though the store has traction now treat it with urgency. Now you're profitable while trying to figure out how to create your own winning creatives that stand out.

no with evidence, not words. And when they are not listening, your community and your lawyer make
them listen.

Healthy balances and consistent business activity.

Clean history from other processors showing low disputes.

Response times, resolution rates, satisfaction scores.

Social Proof

Active social media, real customer reviews, community engagement.

screenshots to your escalation emails. This turns a vague threat into a credible business reality that
risk teams take seriously.

04 — THE 7-METHOD ATTACK FRAMEWORK
────────────────────────────────────────

① METHOD 1 — Formal Support Ticket + Full Documentation
Standard support ticket with your complete proof-of-business arsenal attached. Submit within 24
hours of hold notification.

② METHOD 2 — Live Chat Offensive
2-3 chat sessions per day. Different rep each time. Data-driven, stock proof and tracking ready to
upload.

③ METHOD 3 — Email Support Bombardment
1-2 emails per day to standard support with documentation, metrics, and escalation language.

④ METHOD 4 — Direct Internal Email Campaign
Bypass frontline. Hit department heads and named personnel directly. See Sections 8-9 for
directories.

⑤ METHOD 5 — Daily Phone Calls
Call every number daily. One sympathetic agent can resolve everything. Have metrics memorized.

⑥ METHOD 6 — Legal Pressure
Attorney demand letter after 10-14 days. Even the threat of legal action changes how your case is
handled.

⑦ METHOD 7 — Public Pressure & Social Media Leverage (NEW)
Reference your social media following and community in escalation emails. Signal that you will share
your experience publicly if the matter is not reviewed fairly. This creates reputational pressure that
forces actual human attention on your case. See Section 5.

⚠ THE THREE-PRONGED PRESSURE SYSTEM

Page 5

PAYMENT HOLDS, TERMINATIONS & DISPUTES BIBLE • by Zakaria_Airakaz

Data proves you are legitimate. Legal threats prove you are serious. Public pressure proves they
cannot ignore you. When all three hit the same inbox at the same time, your case gets ACTUALLY
reviewed instead of sitting in a queue.

05 — SOCIAL MEDIA & PUBLIC PRESSURE STRATEGY
────────────────────────────────────────

Payment processors are massive companies with public reputations to protect. When a compliant
merchant with a large, engaged audience signals they are about to share their experience publicly, it
creates a pressure point that internal support channels cannot. This is not about making empty
threats. It is about making your case impossible to ignore.

▸ Why Public Pressure Works
REASON

HOW IT HELPS

Reputational Risk

Processors actively monitor social media for negative mentions. A
viral post from a merchant with 50K+ followers is a PR problem they
want to avoid.

Escalation Trigger

Public pressure pushes cases from frontline queue into executive
review. Senior people get involved faster.

Credibility Signal

A merchant with a large, real audience is clearly running a legitimate
business. The social proof IS the business proof.

Urgency Creator

Standard tickets sit in queues. Tickets with potential public visibility
get priority attention.

▸ The Escalation Language Framework
The key is to be professional, not threatening. You are not saying "I will destroy your reputation." You
are saying "I have a significant community that is already asking about this situation, and I would
prefer to share a positive resolution story." The implication is clear, but the tone remains professional
and constructive.
Soft Pressure (Use in initial escalation emails, Days 5-10)

☑ "As a business with a significant online presence, our community has noticed the disruption to
our operations."
☑ "Several of our [X,000] followers on [Platform] have been asking about the status of our
store/account."
☑ "We would much prefer to share a positive resolution story with our audience."
☑ "Our community trusts us and we want to maintain that trust by resolving this quickly."

Medium Pressure (Use in follow-ups, Days 10-14)

Page 6

PAYMENT HOLDS, TERMINATIONS & DISPUTES BIBLE • by Zakaria_Airakaz

☑ "We have an engaged following of [X,000+] across Twitter, Instagram, and TikTok that is
watching this situation."
☑ "We have been transparent with our community about this experience and the response we
have received so far."
☑ "Multiple content creators in our space have reached out asking about our experience with
[Platform]."
☑ "We are documenting this entire process and intend to share our experience publicly."

Hard Pressure (Use in final escalation emails, Days 14+)

☑ "Our legal counsel has advised us of our rights, and we are prepared to pursue all available
remedies."
☑ "We have [X,000+] followers actively engaged with our brand. We intend to share a detailed
account of this experience across all platforms."
☑ "We are in contact with multiple media outlets and industry journalists covering payment
processor practices."
☑ "We would strongly prefer to resolve this privately and share a positive outcome with our
audience, but we are fully prepared to go public if necessary."

⚠ Rules for Public Pressure
NEVER make threats you cannot back up. Only reference follower counts you actually have. Only
mention legal counsel if you actually have one (or are in the process of engaging one). The power
comes from credibility. One provably false claim destroys all your leverage. Keep it real, keep it
professional, keep it provable.

⚡ Screenshot Everything

When referencing your social presence in emails, ATTACH screenshots showing your actual follower
counts, engagement metrics, and community size. This transforms your leverage from a vague claim
into hard evidence. "We have a large following" is ignorable. A screenshot showing 65,000 Instagram
followers is not.

▸ Combining All Three Pressure Points in One Email
The most effective escalation emails combine data (proving compliance), legal threat (proving
seriousness), and public pressure (proving visibility) in a single communication. Here is the structure:
SECTION

CONTENT

Paragraph 1

Professional opener: who you are, account ID, issue, previous
attempts (ticket numbers)

Paragraph 2

DATA BLOCK: dispute rate, tracking rate, delivery times, stock proof,
supplier docs — all the facts

Paragraph 3

LEGAL SIGNAL: "Our legal counsel has been engaged and is
reviewing this matter. We are prepared to pursue formal remedies."

Page 7

PAYMENT HOLDS, TERMINATIONS & DISPUTES BIBLE • by Zakaria_Airakaz

Paragraph 4

PUBLIC SIGNAL: "As a brand with [X,000+] followers, our community
is watching. We are documenting this process and intend to share
publicly."

Paragraph 5

CONSTRUCTIVE CLOSE: "We strongly prefer a private, positive
resolution and remain committed to compliance. We are asking for a
fair review."

06 — EMAIL BOMBARDMENT STRATEGY
────────────────────────────────────────

Systematic targeting across multiple contacts with escalating pressure. Every email includes data,
documentation, and — from Day 5 onward — social and legal leverage language.

▸ Rotation System with Pressure Escalation
TIMING

PRESSURE LEVEL

Days 1-4

Pure data + documentation emails. Professional, evidence-heavy, no
pressure language. Build your case record.

Days 5-10

Add SOFT social pressure language. "Our community has noticed..."
Attach social proof screenshots.

Days 10-14

Add MEDIUM pressure + legal signals. "Our counsel is reviewing..."
"We are documenting this publicly..."

Days 14+

FULL three-pronged emails. Data + legal demand + public pressure.
Every email to every contact.

▸ What to Attach to EVERY Escalation Email (Day 5+)
☑ Proof of Stock PDF — branded product photos, warehouse shots
☑ Supplier Agreement PDF — signed contract with terms
☑ Stock Purchase Invoices PDF
☑ Tracking Number Export PDF — last 50-100 orders with delivery status
☑ Bank Statement PDF — most recent month
☑ Business Registration PDF
☑ Social Media Screenshots PDF — follower counts across all platforms (NEW)
☑ Community Engagement Screenshots — customer testimonials, positive mentions (NEW)

⚠ Rotation, Not Mass Blast
Pick 2-3 contacts per day. Personalize each email with their name. Reference your case number.
Rotate to different contacts daily. Never BCC 20 people in one email.

▸ Stripe Escalation Email (Days 7+, With Leverage)
Use this after your initial emails have not received a meaningful response. This adds social proof
leverage and legal signals while keeping the data foundation strong.
SUBJECT: Escalation: Unresolved Payout Hold — Account [ACCT_ID] — Requires
Immediate Review
Dear Stripe Risk Team,
I am writing to escalate the unresolved payout hold on account [ACCT_ID]
for [BUSINESS NAME]. We have submitted [NUMBER] previous requests
(Tickets: [LIST]) over the past [X] days without adequate resolution.
COMPLIANCE DATA (unchanged / improved since initial submission):
• Dispute rate: [X.XX]% | Refund rate: [X.XX]%

required by their banking partners to track and resolve all formal complaints. This routes your case to
a different team than standard support. ALWAYS file a formal complaint in parallel with your ticket —
it creates a second pressure track.

Adding "cc: [Attorney Name]" at the bottom of your email — even if it is just your attorney's name —
signals that real legal eyes are on this case. It changes how the email is categorized and routed
internally. Risk teams handle emails with legal cc's differently than standard support requests. This
single line can be the difference between your email sitting in a queue and it getting escalated.

⚠ The Persistence + Pressure Mindset
After 10+ attempts it may feel hopeless. But remember: you are now sending emails with DATA
proving compliance, LEGAL counsel cc'd, and SOCIAL MEDIA leverage attached. That is a
completely different email than what 99% of merchants send. A case with three-pronged pressure
that has been denied by 10 frontline reps will absolutely get a different outcome when it reaches a
senior reviewer. Keep going. You only need ONE yes.

13 — ACCOUNT TERMINATIONS & DETERMINATIONS
────────────────────────────────────────

When a processor closes your account entirely, it is a different fight than a hold. Holds are
temporary. Terminations are presented as final. But "final" does not mean you have no options.
Understanding what actually happened, why, and your rights is the first step to either reversing the
decision or recovering your funds.

Page 22

PAYMENT HOLDS, TERMINATIONS & DISPUTES BIBLE • by Zakaria_Airakaz

▸ Types of Account Closure
TYPE

WHAT IT MEANS

Termination

Account permanently closed. You can no longer process payments.
Usually triggered by policy violations, high dispute rates, or risk
assessment.

Determination

A formal review decision that your business does not meet their
requirements. Often comes after a review period. May include a
reason code.

Suspension

Account frozen but not permanently closed. You may be able to
appeal and get reinstated. Often precedes termination if not resolved.

Restriction / Limitation

Specific capabilities disabled (e.g., payouts paused, new charges
blocked) while account technically remains open. Common with
PayPal.

Reserve + Wind-Down

Account being closed gradually. They hold a reserve from remaining
balance for 90-180 days to cover potential chargebacks, then release.

▸ Why Accounts Get Terminated
REASON

WHAT HAPPENED

High Dispute Rate

Exceeded 0.75-1.0% chargeback threshold. Card networks
(Visa/Mastercard) mandate action. This is the #1 killer.

Prohibited Business Type

Your product category was flagged as restricted or prohibited under
their TOS. Sometimes misclassified.

Risk Assessment Failure

The risk team determined your business model, industry, or
processing pattern represents unacceptable risk.

TOS Violation

Specific terms of service violation identified (misleading descriptions,
unapproved products, etc).

Verification Failure

Could not verify identity, business legitimacy, or documentation did not
pass review.

Fraud Signals

Automated systems flagged suspicious patterns (IP, device,
transaction velocity, etc).

Volume Spike

Sudden increase triggered automated closure before human review.

External Report

Third party (customer, competitor, regulatory body) reported your
business.

⚠ The MATCH List / TMF
When Stripe or another processor terminates you, they may add your business to the MATCH list
(Member Alert to Control High-Risk Merchants), also known as the Terminated Merchant File (TMF).
This is a shared database that other processors check. Being on the MATCH list makes it

Page 23

PAYMENT HOLDS, TERMINATIONS & DISPUTES BIBLE • by Zakaria_Airakaz

significantly harder to get approved by other processors. If you believe you were wrongly terminated,
fighting to get removed from MATCH is critical. This typically requires legal counsel.

▸ Your Rights After Termination
Even after termination, you have rights. Processors cannot simply keep your money forever.
Understanding the legal framework gives you leverage.
RIGHT

WHAT IT MEANS FOR YOU

Right to Your Funds

They must release your funds eventually. Reserve periods are
typically 90-180 days. They cannot keep your money permanently
unless there is a valid legal claim (e.g., outstanding chargebacks).

Right to Explanation

Most processors are required to tell you WHY your account was
closed. If they gave a vague reason, you can demand specifics.

Right to Appeal

Most platforms have an appeal process, even if they do not advertise
it prominently. You have nothing to lose by filing one.

Right to File Complaints

CFPB, BBB, state Attorney General, and card network complaint
processes all exist for this exact situation.

Right to Legal Action

If funds are being withheld beyond the stated reserve period, or if the
termination was unjustified, you have legal recourse.

Right to Data

You can request all data associated with your account, including the
reason for closure. GDPR (EU) and CCPA (CA) strengthen this.

▸ Termination vs Hold: Different Strategy
A hold is about getting them to LOOK at your case. A termination is about getting them to REVERSE
a decision. The pressure tactics are similar (data + legal + public) but the framing is completely
different. With holds, you prove you are compliant and ask for release. With terminations, you
challenge the decision itself and demand reconsideration.
ELEMENT

HOLD APPROACH vs TERMINATION APPROACH

Tone

Hold: "Please review our compliance data." Termination: "This
decision was made in error. Here is the evidence. We demand
reconsideration."

Legal Angle

Hold: "Our counsel is monitoring." Termination: "Our counsel is
preparing formal action including CFPB complaint and potential
litigation."

Public Angle

Hold: "Our community is watching." Termination: "We are prepared to
share our full experience publicly, including the termination decision
and our compliance record."

Urgency

Hold: "We need this resolved promptly." Termination: "We have a
10-day timeline before we proceed with legal and regulatory action."

Page 24

PAYMENT HOLDS, TERMINATIONS & DISPUTES BIBLE • by Zakaria_Airakaz

MATCH/TMF

Not relevant for holds. CRITICAL for terminations. Demand
confirmation of whether you were added to MATCH and demand
removal if unjustified."

14 — TERMINATION APPEAL TEMPLATES
────────────────────────────────────────

These templates are specifically designed for account closures and final determinations. They
challenge the decision, demand specifics, reference legal rights, and deploy the three-pronged
pressure system. Adapt to your specific platform.

▸ Stripe Termination Appeal
SUBJECT: Formal Appeal: Account Termination — [ACCT_ID] — [BUSINESS NAME]
Dear Stripe Risk Team / Senior Review,
I am formally appealing the termination of account [ACCT_ID] for
[BUSINESS NAME], communicated on [DATE]. We believe this decision
was made in error and request immediate reconsideration.
REASON GIVEN: [Quote their exact termination reason]
WHY THIS DECISION IS INCORRECT:
• Dispute rate at time of closure: [X.XX]% (below all thresholds)
• Total orders processed: [NUMBER] | 100% fulfilled with tracking
• Delivery confirmation rate: [X]% | Avg delivery: [X] days
• Active chargeback alerts: Ethoca + Verifi enrolled
• CS response time: under [X] hours | Zero unresolved complaints
• Real branded inventory on hand (photos attached)
• Active supplier agreements (attached)
• Clean processing history of [X] months
SPECIFIC CHALLENGES TO THEIR STATED REASON:
[Address each point of their termination reason with specific data
that contradicts it. Be detailed and factual.]
LEGAL: Our legal counsel has been retained and is reviewing this
termination. We have been advised to pursue formal remedies including
CFPB complaint, state AG complaint, and potential litigation for
wrongful termination and unlawful fund retention. Our counsel has
also requested confirmation of whether [BUSINESS NAME] has been
added to the MATCH/TMF list, and is prepared to pursue removal
if the termination basis is unjustified.
PUBLIC: [BUSINESS NAME] has an engaged community of [X,000+]

Page 25

PAYMENT HOLDS, TERMINATIONS & DISPUTES BIBLE • by Zakaria_Airakaz

followers. We are documenting this termination and our compliance
record for public disclosure. We strongly prefer a private reversal.
FORMAL REQUESTS:
1. Detailed written explanation of the specific basis for termination
2. Reconsideration and reinstatement of the account
3. Immediate release of all held funds ($[AMOUNT])
4. Confirmation of MATCH/TMF listing status
5. If reinstatement is denied, a written final determination with

15 — FUND RECOVERY AFTER TERMINATION
────────────────────────────────────────

Even if you cannot get the account reinstated, you CAN and MUST get your money back.
Processors cannot keep your funds permanently. This section covers how to force release of held
funds after account closure.

▸ Fund Recovery Timeline
TIMELINE

ACTION

Days 1-7

File termination appeal (Section 14). Request fund release as part of
the appeal. File formal complaint through the platform's complaint
portal.

Days 7-14

If no response: file CFPB complaint (consumerfinance.gov). File BBB
complaint. Contact state AG consumer protection division.

Days 14-21

Attorney demand letter specifically requesting fund release with
deadline. Reference regulatory complaints already filed.

Days 21-30

Full three-pronged pressure: legal demand + CFPB escalation +
public disclosure of fund retention.

Days 30-90

If reserve period applies, monitor timeline. Document every day past
the stated release date that funds are not returned.

Days 90-180

Standard reserve periods end. If funds are not released, attorney files
formal legal action for fund recovery.

Day 180+

Any funds still held beyond stated reserve period = potential unlawful
fund retention. Legal action strongly warranted.

▸ Platform-Specific Fund Recovery
PLATFORM

FUND RECOVERY DETAILS

Stripe

Stripe typically holds a reserve for 90-120 days after closure. After the
reserve period, remaining balance should be paid out to your bank

Page 29

PAYMENT HOLDS, TERMINATIONS & DISPUTES BIBLE • by Zakaria_Airakaz

account. If it is not, file a CFPB complaint AND have your attorney
send a demand letter.
Shopify

Shopify Payments holds funds for 120 days after termination. After
120 days, net balance is released minus any chargebacks. If not
released, escalate through the internal contact directory + CFPB.

PayPal

PayPal holds funds for up to 180 days after permanent limitation. This
is the longest standard hold period. After 180 days, you can withdraw
remaining balance. If they refuse, CFPB + attorney.

PAYMENT HOLDS, TERMINATIONS & DISPUTES BIBLE • by Zakaria_Airakaz

▸ Regulatory Complaint Quick Reference
AGENCY

HOW TO FILE & WHAT IT DOES

CFPB

consumerfinance.gov/complaint — File under "Money transfers,
virtual currency, or money service." Include all documentation.
Processors must respond within 15 days.

BBB

bbb.org/file-a-complaint — File against the processor's legal entity.
Include timeline, amounts, and documentation. Creates public record.

State Attorney General

Search "[YOUR STATE] attorney general consumer complaint" — File
with the AG in YOUR state AND the processor's state (California for
Stripe, Delaware for Shopify/PayPal).

Card Network Complaints

Visa: visa.com/merchant-complaints | Mastercard:
mastercard.com/merchant — If MATCH listing is unjustified, dispute
through card networks.

FTC

reportfraud.ftc.gov — If you believe the processor engaged in unfair
or deceptive practices. Creates federal record.

✅ The CFPB Is Your Most Powerful Weapon

The Consumer Financial Protection Bureau requires companies to respond to complaints within 15
days. This is a federal regulatory deadline they cannot ignore. Filing a CFPB complaint moves your
case from "customer service" to "regulatory compliance" inside the processor's organization. For fund
recovery after termination, a CFPB complaint combined with an attorney demand letter is the single
most effective strategy.

▸ MATCH List / TMF Removal
If you were added to the MATCH list, getting removed is critical for your ability to process payments
anywhere in the future. The acquirer (processor) that added you is the only entity that can remove
you. MATCH entries expire after 5 years if not removed.

☑ Request WRITTEN confirmation from the processor of whether you were added to MATCH
☑ If yes, demand the specific reason code used for the MATCH entry
☑ Challenge the reason code with evidence (same documentation package you have been
using)
☑ Have your attorney send a formal demand for MATCH removal citing the unjustified basis
☑ If the processor refuses, escalate through card network dispute processes (Visa/Mastercard)
☑ File CFPB complaint specifically referencing unjustified MATCH listing
☑ Document everything — MATCH removal disputes can take months but are worth pursuing
☑ Consider engaging a specialized payments attorney for MATCH disputes

Page 31

PAYMENT HOLDS, TERMINATIONS & DISPUTES BIBLE • by Zakaria_Airakaz

⚠ Moving Forward After Termination
Even if you cannot reverse the termination, you can still process payments. Apply to alternative
processors: Adyen, Checkout.com, Square, Authorize.net, or high-risk processors like Durango
Merchant Services, PayKickstart, or eMerchantBroker. Be upfront about the previous termination and
have your compliance documentation ready. If you were NOT added to MATCH, most processors will
approve you. If you WERE added, high-risk processors specialize in MATCH-listed merchants.

DATA PROVES IT. YOUR LAWYER DEMANDS IT. YOUR AUDIENCE IS
WATCHING.
Holds, terminations, and determinations — same playbook: compliance proof + legal threat +
public visibility.
Make it impossible for them to ignore your case. Get your money. Get your account.

Product Research MasterClass
by Zakaria_Airakaz ​
WHAT IS A WINNER PRODUCT?
For me, the whole idea of a winning product that most gurus and Ecom-discord groups
are talking about is false/wrong
(a winner product is the product that you will get after testing what was before 10
products and now 100 products and it will give you 3 Roas for the first 3 days and then
you can start scaling to 1k$/day and keep testing new products to get more winners so
you finally can scale your store to 100k$/m)
How can this strategy be wrong if it can allow you to scale to 100k/m?

Because this strategy doesn't teaches you shit but it turns you into a hard-working VA
for yourself

Now let me break down to you how

●​ You are copying other people's winners: Which means you don't even know
why that product is a winner, you don’t know which desire it satisfies, why the
product page works, why the offer works, and why their ads work, and how they
make the product fit in the market ​
●​ You are at the mercy of luck: if you are copying products that already
thousands of people are copying too means all you have is luck for things to work
for you and see some success​
●​ Keep testing and testing more: this is basically when you turn to a VA that
turns off his brain and keeps doing the same things over and over until he gets
lucky and looks for more winners
Results? Two scenarios ​
First, you get lucky find a winner make some profit test more products find more winners
until the competition gets tougher, leaving you without a real business.
You get unlucky, lose all your money, and decide eCom is a scam. You give up and go
back to your old life, leaving your dreams behind.

In both scenarios, you will get fucked up

And you are not gay so you do not want to get fucked right?
By now, you’re probably wondering: if spam-testing products aren’t the answer, then
what is? ​
​
Understand the first question we start this doc with WHAT IS A WINNER PRODUCT?
And it is quite simple a winner product is a product that satisfies a mass desire means
an I want … that is shared by millions of people either all around the world or in a
specific country
●​ I want to lose weight
●​ I want my hair back
●​ I want to walk pain-free
●​ I want my dog to be health
●​ I want my kids to do well in school
●​ I want to get the girl of my dream
●​ I want my assurance to cover my medical bill (specifically for the USA)
Now we know what is the real answer to What Is A Winner Product

Does that mean you can just look for a product that satisfies a mass desire and start
selling it? The answer is no
Because theirs scales to how easy or hard to sell a winning product and that comes to :

●​ The Magnitude of Desire: this is what defines how much a person is willing to
do to satisfy his desire and that comes to the impact of not satisfying his desire
on him
Physically like:
○​ People overweight lose their mobility
○​ Increased risk of serious health conditions like heart disease or diabetes.
Or mentally like :
○​ Low Self-Esteem
○​ Shame and Guilt

​
So the product that you should be looking for should be the answer to satisfy a
powerful desire​
​

●​ What Level Of Awareness The Market Is On:

The higher on the scale the harder to sell to it requires more effort compared to
the bottom of the scale meaning:

●​ If you’re trying to sell to people who are unaware they have a problem or a
desire to fulfill, it requires significant effort to persuade them. As a cold
audience, they don’t recognize the issue, so convincing them to buy a
product to solve something they don’t acknowledge is a challenging uphill
battle.​
●​ On the other hand, selling to people who are further down the awareness
scale, such as those who are solution-aware or product-aware, is much
easier. These individuals are already in the market, actively searching for
a solution or even a specific product to fulfill their desires. As a result,
convincing them requires significantly less effort compared to targeting an
unaware audience.
This means that if you’re just starting, it’s better to focus on products where the market
awareness is already at the Solution-Aware or Product-Aware stage. These audiences
are actively seeking solutions or specific products, making it easier to capture their
interest and drive sales compared to targeting a Problem-Aware or Unaware market.

●​ How Much Is The Competition (Market Sophistication): This refers to how
many competitors are out there trying to satisfy the same desire. The more
sophisticated the market, the harder it is to stand out, as customers are saying
multiple ads for the same desire.

​

This means if you can enter the market with a product that fulfills a desire no one else
has addressed before, you could make an incredible amount of money with relative
ease. However, let’s be honest—this is a rare, once-in-a-lifetime opportunity that only a
few people ever achieve. And to be real with you, I’m not one of them.
I’ve never aspired to be the next Elon Musk or reinvent the wheel.

A great example is Davie Fogarty, the creator of The Oodie. He entered his niche
extremely early, allowing the brand to scale to a massive $500M in revenue. His
success wasn’t just luck—he identified a barely tapped market and executed brilliantly.
That said, his early entry played a significant role in achieving such extraordinary
results.

But let’s be clear: you don’t have to wait around for the next untapped market or a
revolutionary desire that no one has solved.

But I explained this to know how to market Sophistication plays a role in making the
product easy to sell

Weight Loss
Is on market sophistication level 5 :
●​ The weight loss market has been heavily saturated for years, and customers
have seen countless claims, mechanisms, and promises.
●​ Many no longer believe in "miracle solutions" and are highly skeptical of any
product or claim.
●​ Success in this market requires advanced marketing strategies, such as deep
emotional storytelling, leveraging social proof, and building trust over time, rather
than relying on bold claims or standard mechanisms.

But there is one truth that everyone agrees on exercise makes you lose weight

An example to talk about: is the ring that helps you lose weight

How did the Infinity Hoop fight the niche saturation and overcome the audience's
exhaustion?

The market saturation came from that theirs too many competitors selling solutions for
weight loss:
●​ Supplement
●​ Special diets
●​ Exercises
●​ Etc…
And if you did some simple research about people on the weight loss journey you would
find that 99% of them lack the willpower and self-discipline to start training
And have been tired of trying those magic tricks that don’t deliver any results
So this brand has to deal with two main objections:
●​ Does using this product will get me the results that I want?
●​ Will it be easy to stick to compared with gym, running, and other stuff that
requires discipline and willpower that I don’t have?

How they did it:
●​ Social proof shows their avatar's journey getting the results that they
dream about while using the product
●​ Focusing their ads on showing people having fun while getting the results
that they want
And this happened because they have a product that has a unique feature that allows
you to burn calories and exercise while having fun​
​
​
Their ads: Facebook library

There's no magical product research method that guarantees you success. It's not about the product research method that guarantees you the brand. It's not true. Regardless of where you found the product, through Aliexpress, Facebook, wherever else, TikTok, you can make it work. As long as it fits a few criteria. People always ask you, what are the winning niches you're going to now? Doesn't matter. In Evolve, there's like 300 dudes. Inside, I've seen dudes crush it with brands from different niches. Supplements. Fashion. A whole lot of different ones also. Doesn't matter. Second thing. A lot of you guys will have been told, if you guys have purchased info from elsewhere before, pay 10k for some dude to tell you to copy paste. Spam testing is BS. non-GMO

choices.

Similar Product Research​

​
The goal of Similar Product Research is to deeply understand what our ideal
customer loves and hates about products most similar to ours
This research helps us:
●​ Pinpoint what features, benefits, and promises actually excite the market
(what to highlight in ads and on-page)​

●​ Identify Hidden objections or annoyances (what to overcome proactively in our
messaging)​
●​ Uncover opportunities to create ad concepts around “we fixed what others
missed”​

📌 For example:​

If customers love that a supplement uses natural ingredients…​
…but they hate that it’s not FDA-approved, has hidden fillers, or includes sugar
—

👉

We position our product with:​
“Clinically Clean. FDA-Registered. 100% Natural — with Zero Fillers or Added
Sugar.”
→ This highlights the same desirable qualities they’re already looking for,​
but removes the objections that made them hesitate with other brands.

AI PROMPT
Hi, I want you to act as a world-class creative strategist for a $100M/year direct
response brand in the HAIR LOSS PCOS
You will be analyzing raw customer reviews, discussions, and testimonials from people
who have purchased or used products very similar to ours. These are real users
expressing their unfiltered thoughts.
Your task is to extract powerful, emotional, and insight-rich responses by answering the
following questions:

1. What Do They Love About These Similar Products?

⚠️ Important:​

Do not focus on outcomes or benefits like “it worked” or “I saw a difference.”​
We're not looking for transformations or results in this section.

🎯 Instead, focus only on what customers love about the product itself, such as:

●​ Materials, ingredients, or components they like or trust​
●​ Ease of use (e.g. easy to apply, simple to set up, comfortable to wear)​
●​ Design, form factor, or usability features​
●​ Quality of construction, packaging, or delivery experience​
●​ Safety, cleanliness, certifications, or trust signals (e.g. FDA-approved,
eco-friendly, made in the USA)​
●​ Convenience factors like dosing, size, portability, or how well it fits into daily
routines​
●​ Anything that makes the product feel premium, thoughtful, or confidence-inspiring​

🗣 Use exact customer phrases where possible to capture real, emotional language
​

2. What Do They Hate or Complain About in These Products?
Look for:
●​ Side effects​
●​ Lack of results​
●​ Dosage or price concerns​
●​ Packaging, taste, or trust issues
●​ etc​

Use exact phrases and emotional language to capture objections

3. What Desires or Expectations Are These Products Failing to Meet?
What’s still missing for them? What are they hoping these products would fix but didn’t?
This helps identify gaps to position our solution as the one that “finally
delivers”

4. What Messaging, Features, or Angles Can We Use to Stand Out?
Based on the avatar’s frustrations and unmet expectations:
●​ What could we emphasize?​
●​ What pain point can we fix better?​
●​ What feature or ingredient can we claim more confidently?​

5. What Objections Should We Preemptively Handle?
These are points we’ll want to address in our:
●​ Product page​
●​ FAQ​
●​ Guarantee/Trust copy​
●​ Ads (to remove friction)​

The Ultimate SOP for Building
High-Converting Landing Page By
Zakaria_Airakaz
Bonus At The End How To Be A Great Copywriter
1. The Mission, the Philosophy of a Landing Page :

The true mission of a landing page is to guide a cold visitor through a
belief-shifting journey that leads to a confident, self-driven buying decision.
It’s not about hard selling — it’s about building emotional and logical
alignment so that the prospect feels like the decision was theirs all along.
A powerful landing page:
● Converts cold traffic into high-intent buyers
● Increases AOV by elevating perceived value, not lowering price
● Builds trust by using psychology, not pressure
● Shifts beliefs across five key dimensions:
○ the problem
○ failed past solutions,
○ your solution
○ social proof
○ urgency

It works because it aligns with how the brain actually makes decisions —
using principles like:
● System 1 & 2 Thinking (emotion + logic) by Daniel

Kahneman
○ our brains have two modes when it make decisions:

System 1 – The Fast, Feeling Brain
This is the part of your brain that works super fast.
It makes quick choices based on feelings, pictures, and
stories. You use it when:
● A hero background story that feels related to you
● You see a yummy cake and want it right away
● You like a product because it “feels right”
● Emotional appeal: Show happy customers, lifestyle benefits then
you smile or imagine yourself getting results
● You see Familiarity and trust: recognizable logos, badges (like
“100% Money Back Guarantee” or “Trusted by 1,000,000+
Customers”), and consistent branding.
System 1 = emotions, gut feeling, fast decisions

System 2 – The Slow, Thinking Brain
This part is slower but smarter.
It helps you think, solve problems, and make careful choices.
You use it when:
● You read the details before buying something: The root cause,
The unique mechanism of the solution
● You think, “Is this really worth it?”
● You compare two products to choose the better one, or your
mind thinks about similar products and how much they
cost:
● Use Feature Comparison Tables
● Cost-Benefit Framing

�� System 2 = logic, facts, slow and smart decisions

�� Good landing pages use both:
● First, they catch your emotions with pictures, stories, and strong
headlines (System 1)
● Then, they explain why it makes sense to buy with facts and
proof (System 2)

That’s how they help people say:
“I want this!” and “This makes sense!”

● Self-Determination Theory – Why People Really Do Things:
○ People are more likely to do something (like buy a product or try
something new) when three big needs are met:
■ 1. Autonomy – “I want to choose this myself”
People don’t like being bossed around.
They want to feel like they made the decision, not that
someone forced them.
�� Example:
“I picked this on my own — it feels right for me.

● 2. Competence – “I believe I can do this”
People take action when they feel capable and confident.
If something looks too hard or confusing, they’ll back away.
�� Example:
“This looks easy enough… I can totally do it!”

● 3. Connection – “This is made for someone like me”
People like to feel understood and accepted.
They want to see that the brand or product “gets” them.
�� Example:
“This feels like it was made for people just like me!”

�� What Great Landing Pages Do:
● They let you feel like you’re in control (autonomy)
● They make things feel simple and doable (competence)
● They talk to you in a way that feels friendly and familiar (connection)

That’s how they make people feel safe, smart, and excited to buy — without
pressure.

● COM-B Model (capability, opportunity, motivation):

COM-B is a way to understand why people do things (like buying a product or
starting something new).
It says people need three things to take action:
1. Capability – “Can I do this?”
People need to feel able to do it.
If it looks too hard or confusing, they won’t try.
�� Example:

“I understand how this works — I think I can do it.”

2. Opportunity – “Is this possible right now?”
Even if someone wants to do it, they need the chance.
If it’s out of stock, too expensive, or not available to them, they’ll walk
away.
�� Example:
“It’s available, it fits my budget, and it ships to me — nice!”

3. Motivation – “Do I even want this?”
People won’t take action unless they really want the result.
The product has to solve a problem they care about.
�� Example:
“This is exactly what I’ve been looking for!”

�� What Great Landing Pages Do:
● They make it easy to understand (capability)
● They remove friction (opportunity)
● They connect emotionally and show benefits (motivation)

When all 3 are in place → people take action naturally.

● Narrative Transportation & Identity Theory (story and
self-image drive behavior)
○ People don’t just remember facts — they remember stories.And they
don’t just buy products — they buy transformations.

People See Themselves as the Hero
Everyone wants to be the main character in their own
story. They want to go from struggling → to winning.
From feeling stuck → to feeling proud.
�� Example:
“I used to feel embarrassed about my skin… but now I’m in love with it.”

Stories Help People Imagine Results
A good story helps people picture their life with your
product. It makes them feel what it would be like to win.
�� Example:
“This mom used to wake up in pain — now she plays with her kids
every morning. I want that too.”
�� What Great Landing Pages Do:
● Tell before-and-after stories
● Share real journeys from people like the buyer
● Help visitors see themselves winning

Stories = emotion.
Emotion = action.
That’s why stories sell way better than stats.

● Processing Fluency, Anticipated Regret, and Anchoring
(shape perceived value and action)

1. Processing Fluency – “This Feels Easy to Understand”

People are more likely to trust and buy something if it’s easy to
read, watch, or understand.
If your page feels simple, smooth, and clean — they feel smart and safe.
�� Example:
“This looks so clear… I get it right away.”
Why it matters:
● Makes people feel confident
● Reduces confusion or doubt
● Speeds up decisions

�� On Landing Pages:
Use big text, clear headlines, short sentences, clean design.
If they can skim it and still feel like they understand — you win.

2. Anticipated Regret – “What If I Don’t Do This… And
Regret It Later?”
What it means:
Before people act, they imagine how they’ll feel if they don’t act. If
they picture missing out or feeling bad later, they’re more likely to
buy now.
�� Example:
“I don’t want to wait and then wish I had started sooner.”
Why it matters:
● Creates emotional urgency
● Helps people think long-term
● Makes the product feel more important

�� On Landing Pages:

Use lines like:
● “Most people regret waiting”
● “You don’t want to look back in 6 months and wish you started
today”
●
That thought moves people to act.

3. Anchoring – “Is This a Good Price? Compared to What?”
What it means:
People judge value by comparing it to something else. You
“anchor” their mind by showing a higher number first, so your
price feels like a great deal.
�� Example:
“This was $299 — now it’s just $79!”
Why it matters:
● Makes your price feel like a steal
● Shapes how big or small a number feels
● Increases perceived value

�� On Landing Pages:
● Show the original price vs discounted price
● Compare your product to expensive alternatives
● Show everything they’re getting (bonus stack) before showing
price

Anchoring boosts perceived value and makes buying feel smart.

Summary: How These 3 Boost Conversions
1. Processing Fluency
→ Make the experience feel smooth and easy
→ People say “Yes” faster when their brain doesn’t have to work
hard
2. Anticipated Regret
→ Trigger fear of missing out or wishing they started sooner
→ Creates urgency and emotional push
3. Anchoring
→ Shape how your price is seen by comparing it
→ Makes your offer feel like a no-brainer

● Showing the Worst-Case If They Don’t Act Loss Aversion
(from Behavioral Economics) similar to the one above
(Anticipated Regret)
People fear loss more than they value gain.
So if you show them how things could get worse — and fast — if they don’t
take action, it creates urgency and moves them out of procrastination.
Example:
“Most women don’t even realize they’re losing 15–20 hairs a day
until it’s too late… the root damage is already happening under the
skin.”
Why it works:
● Adds urgency and a ticking clock
● Makes the pain feel real and risky

● Forces them to confront the cost of doing nothing
● Increases perceived value of your solution (prevention is priceless)

How important is this?
Very important. Without it, people delay. With it, they act now to avoid pain.

● Showing the Perfect Life (Results Over Time) Future Pacing
You show them what life could look like — week 1, week 3, week 6 — by
letting them visually and emotionally experience the transformation in their
mind.
You’re not just saying “This works” — you’re letting them feel the journey.
Example:
“By Week 1, the bloating was gone. By Week 3, my hair stopped
shedding. And by Week 6… I felt confident looking in the mirror
again.”
Why it works:
● Triggers visualization of their own success
● Uses mirror neurons (they imagine it happening to them)
● Shifts focus from fear to hope → increases buying desire
● It makes the result feel real, measurable, and inevitable

How important is this?
Extremely powerful. This is how you get people emotionally invested in the
outcome. It activates System 1 (emotion) + System 2 (timeline logic). Perfect
combo.

● Externalizing the Problem Creating a Devil (a Villain)
People naturally try to understand why they’re in pain or stuck. If you don’t

give them a clear reason, they’ll blame themselves — and when people feel
ashamed, they freeze and don’t buy.
So instead, you give them a villain — a believable, external force that caused
their pain (not them).
This creates relief, clarity, and motivation.
It’s not your fault — it’s:
● your hormones (PCOS)
● the broken system (Big Pharma, fake skincare, sugar
industry)
● your past habits (you were never taught the right way)
● your environment (stress, toxins, low light exposure)

Why it works:
● Removes shame → reduces internal resistance
● Creates us vs them tension → Boosts engagement
● Makes your solution feel like a heroic escape

How important is this?
Crucial. Without a villain, people feel lost or blame themselves — and that
kills action.
With a villain, they feel seen, empowered, and ready to fight back — with your
product.

Unlike generic product pages or hard-sell tactics, landing pages that follow
this philosophy:
● 2–4x conversion rates (CVR)
● Significantly higher AOV
● Lower refund Lower impulse buy
● Create movement, not just sales

Your landing page isn’t just a sales tool — it’s a system that earns
belief, builds trust, and makes conversion feel inevitable.

2. High-Level Structure / Blueprint
Here’s the basic skeleton of a proven LP framework used in Meta
ads: 1. Hero Section
2. Background Story
3. Problem Amplification
4. Root Cause + Villain
5. Unique Mechanism (Solution Reveal)
6. Product Reveal + Features
7. Social Proof (Round 1)

8. Offer Stack
9. Transformation Timeline
10. Final CTA
11. Objection Handling / FAQs
12. Social Proof (Round 2)

3. Section-by-Section Breakdown:
1. HERO SECTION – Emotional Hook:
● Primary Purpose:
Capture instant emotional attention (System 1), create curiosity, and
make the visitor feel:
“That’s me. I need this.”

What’s Really Happening Here (Psychologically)
You're speaking to the fast, emotional, impulsive part of the brain (System 1):
● It does not read long paragraphs.
● It makes decisions based on vibes, images, gut feeling, color, facial
expressions, and clarity.
● It answers:
“Does this feel good?”
“Do I relate?”
“Do I want this life?”
If System 1 says “Yes,” the visitor scrolls.
If it says “Meh,” they bounce — no matter how good the rest of the page is.

❓
❓
